## What was accomplished:

### Feature #260: Keyboard Bulk Node Movement (PASSING)
- Added moveNodes batch method to coreStore.ts:
  - Takes array of {nodeId, x, y} moves and optional snapshot description
  - Applies all moves to graph in sequence using engineMoveNode
  - Clamps coordinates to Math.max(0, value) to prevent negative positions
  - Takes single undo snapshot after all moves complete
  - Updates isDirty, canUndo, canRedo state
- Added Alt+Arrow keyboard handler in Canvas.tsx:
  - Alt+Arrow: moves selected nodes by 20px (SMALL_STEP)
  - Shift+Alt+Arrow: moves selected nodes by 100px (LARGE_STEP)
  - Uses capture phase event listener
  - Skips when text input focused, dialogs open, Connect mode, placement mode
  - Builds batch moves from current graph positions of selected nodes
  - Calls moveNodes with formatted description "Move N node(s)"
- Added CSS transition in index.css:
  - .react-flow__node { transition: transform 150ms ease-out }
  - .react-flow__node.dragging { transition: none } (disables during drag)

  nested navigation, getAllCommands integration

  - Added toastMessage/toastTimerId state + showToast/clearToast actions to uiStore
  - Created src/components/shared/Toast.tsx component (fixed bottom-center, auto-dismiss 4s)
  - Added <Toast /> to App.tsx

  - Added Enter key confirmation (keyboard accessible)
  - Added toast after deletion: "Deleted {name}. Cmd+Z to undo"
- Added edge deletion via Delete key in Canvas.tsx (direct, no confirmation)
- Fixed critical mode filter bug in useKeyboardShortcuts.ts:
  - Old: `if (actionId.startsWith('edit:') && currentMode !== CanvasMode.Edit) return;`
  - New: `if (actionId === 'edit:exit' && currentMode !== CanvasMode.Edit) return;`
  - This was blocking edit:undo, edit:redo, edit:delete in Normal mode
- 18 unit tests in test/unit/ui/keyboardDeletionWithUndo.test.ts
- Browser verified: node delete+toast+undo, edge delete+toast all working

## Key bug fixes:
- Mode filter was overly broad, blocking ALL edit:* actions in Normal mode.
  Only edit:exit (the mode transition action) should be gated by mode.
  Category-based actions (edit:undo, edit:redo, edit:delete) work in ALL modes.

  9. Feature #227 Step 4-6: modify/re-save, updated_at changes, created_at stays

SESSION: 2026-03-03 - Feature #214
==================================================

## What was accomplished:

### Feature #214: Double-click Add Note doesn't create duplicate notes (PASSING)
- Added useRef-based savingNoteRef guard in NotesTab component (NodeDetailPanel.tsx)
- The guard prevents handleSave from executing twice on rapid double-click:
  - First Save: sets savingNoteRef.current = true, calls onAddNote, closes editor
  - Second Save: savingNoteRef.current is true → returns immediately (no duplicate)
- Guard lifecycle:
  - Resets to false on handleOpenEditor (new editor session)
  - Resets to false on handleCancel (so next note creation works)
  - Stays true after save until editor opens again (prevents race condition)
- Also added useRef import to the file's React import line

SESSION: 2026-03-03 - Feature #212
==================================================

## What was accomplished:

### Feature #212: Double-click save doesn't corrupt file (PASSING)
- Added `isSaving` boolean guard flag to coreStore state
- Guard prevents concurrent saves from double-click or rapid Ctrl+S:
  - saveFile() checks `if (get().isSaving) return false` at entry
  - saveFileAs() checks the same guard at entry
  - Both methods set `isSaving: true` before starting, reset to `false` on success/error/cancel
  - Cross-method protection: saveFile blocks saveFileAs and vice versa
- Console logs "[CoreStore] Save already in progress, ignoring duplicate request" when rejecting duplicate save

## Test file: test/unit/store/doubleClickSave.test.ts (19 tests, all passing)
1. isSaving starts as false
2. isSaving becomes true while save is in progress
3. Second saveFile() call returns false while first is in progress
4. saveArchcFile is called only once when save is triggered twice rapidly
5. isSaving resets to false after successful save
6. isSaving resets to false after failed save
7. Can save again after first save completes
8. Can save again after first save fails
9. Second saveFileAs() call returns false while first is in progress
10. saveArchcFileAs is called only once for rapid double-click
11. isSaving resets to false after saveFileAs user cancels
12. isSaving resets to false after saveFileAs error
13. saveFileAs blocked while saveFile is in progress
14. saveFile blocked while saveFileAs is in progress
15. isDirty is correctly cleared after single save succeeds
16. isDirty remains true when second save is rejected
17. Graph state remains consistent after rapid save attempts
18. Three rapid saves only execute one save operation
19. Console logs message when duplicate save is rejected

## Browser verification steps completed:
1. Loaded ecommerce.archc: 5 nodes, 4 edges, ✓ Saved ✓
2. Created new file (Ctrl+N) ✓
3. Added Service node → Nodes: 1, ● Modified ✓
4. Pressed Ctrl+S twice rapidly → no crashes, no errors ✓
5. Console: 0 errors, 0 warnings ✓
6. Reloaded ecommerce.archc → all 5 nodes, 4 edges intact ✓
7. Mock data grep: only legitimate globalThis.crypto in codec.ts ✓

## Implementation approach:
- Store-level `isSaving` flag is the simplest and most reliable approach
- Checked at the very start of saveFile() and saveFileAs() (before any async work)
- Uses synchronous Zustand state updates for immediate lock acquisition
- Properly cleared in all code paths (try/catch/finally equivalent)
- No debouncing needed — just a boolean guard that blocks concurrent saves

SESSION: 2026-03-02 - Features #145, #146, #147
==================================================

## What was accomplished:

### Feature #145: Node deletion via Delete/Backspace key (PASSING)
- Added Delete and Backspace key handlers to Canvas component
- Delete key always triggers deletion dialog when a node is selected
- Backspace triggers deletion at root level (zooms out when in navigation path)
- Disabled React Flow's built-in deleteKeyCode to prevent conflicts
- Used capture-phase event listener for reliable key interception
- Ignores keystrokes in input/textarea fields
- Prevents double-trigger when dialog is already open

### Feature #146: Deletion confirmation dialog shows cascade impact (PASSING)
- Created DeleteConfirmationDialog component in src/components/shared/
- Shows node name being deleted (bold)
- Yellow alert box showing cascade impact: N connected edges, N child nodes
- Cancel and Confirm (Delete) buttons with clear visual hierarchy
- Escape key closes dialog, backdrop click closes dialog
- "This action can be undone with Ctrl+Z" message
- Alert triangle warning icon
- z-100 overlay with semi-transparent backdrop

### Feature #147: Node deletion removes connected edges (PASSING)
- Graph engine's removeNode() already handled cascading edge removal
- Created deletionImpact utility (src/core/graph/deletionImpact.ts) for calculating impact
- Verified: Deleting API Gateway (2 edges) → 5→4 nodes, 4→2 edges
- Verified: Deleting Order Service (2 edges) → 5→4 nodes, 4→2 edges
- Other connected nodes preserved correctly

## Technical details:
- Key insight: React Flow v12 has deleteKeyCode='Backspace' by default, which intercepts
  Backspace before custom handlers. Fixed with deleteKeyCode={null} on ReactFlow component.
- Capture-phase event listener (addEventListener('keydown', handler, true)) ensures our
  handler runs before React Flow's internal event handling.
- uiStore extended with deleteDialogOpen/deleteDialogInfo state management.
- DeleteConfirmationDialog uses Zustand stores: useUIStore for dialog state, useCoreStore
  for removeNode action, useCanvasStore for clearing selection after deletion.

- Features passing: 67+ of 235 (~28.5%)
- Zero console errors
- All implementations verified via browser automation on Playwright

  - Rejects version > FORMAT_VERSION with CodecError
  - Error message: "Unsupported format version: {X}. This file was created with a newer version of ArchCanvas. Please update ArchCanvas to the latest version to open this file. (Current max supported version: {FORMAT_VERSION})"
  - Version check happens BEFORE checksum verification (even with skipChecksumVerification)
  - readFormatVersion() utility to inspect version without full decode
- Test fixture: public/future-version.archc (version 9999, ARCHC\0 magic bytes)
- Test file: test/unit/store/formatVersionValidation.test.ts (14 tests, all passing)
  1. Rejects version 9999
  2. Error includes version number "9999"
  3. Error mentions "update"
  4. Error mentions "newer version"
  5. Error includes max supported version
  6. Rejects FORMAT_VERSION + 1
  7. Rejects 65535 (max uint16)
  8. Rejects 256
  9. Does NOT reject current FORMAT_VERSION
  10. Does NOT reject version 0
  11. readFormatVersion reads future version correctly
  12. readFormatVersion reads current version correctly
  13. Thrown error is CodecError instance
  14. Version check before checksum verification

  (e.g., "Malformed protobuf data: header.formatVersion: integer expected")
- Created comprehensive test file: test/unit/store/malformedProtoValidation.test.ts (28 tests)

## Test coverage (28 tests):
1. Wire-level corruption: invalid wire types (3 tests)
   - Wire type 7 on unknown field → CodecError
   - Wire type 6 on unknown field → CodecError
   - Meaningful error message for invalid wire type
2. Wire-level corruption: excessive field lengths (2 tests)
   - Embedded message length exceeds buffer → CodecError
   - String field length exceeds buffer → CodecError
3. Field type mismatches: string where number expected (2 tests)
   - FileHeader format_version as string → CodecError
   - Architecture name as varint → CodecError
4. Structural corruption: nested message issues (2 tests)
   - Corrupted nested Node position → error or safe decode
   - Edge with impossibly large enum value → handled safely
5. Post-decode verify() catches type mismatches (6 tests)
   - Non-integer format_version → "header.formatVersion: integer expected"
   - Non-string architecture name → "name: string expected"
   - Non-array nodes field → "nodes: array expected"
   - Non-string Node.id → "id: string expected"
   - Non-number Position.x → "number expected"
   - Valid message → null (no error)
6. Codec verify integration (2 tests)
   - Valid file passes both decode and verify
   - Protobuf decode errors wrapped as CodecError
7. All malformation errors are proper Error instances (4 tests)
   - Invalid wire type → Error subclass
   - Excessive length → Error subclass
   - Deeply nested corruption → Error subclass, no crash
   - Multiple sequential variants → all proper errors
8. Error messages identify the malformed area (3 tests)
   - verify error includes field path (e.g., "header.formatVersion")
   - Nested node field includes full path
   - Codec decode error includes protobuf context
9. User-visible error dialog integration (2 tests)
   - Malformed data maps to "Invalid File Format" dialog
   - Error dialog dismissible, app continues
10. Round-trip validation (2 tests)
    - Valid file passes both decode and verify
    - Empty architecture passes verify

SESSION: 2026-03-03 - Feature #250
==================================================

## What was accomplished:

### Feature #250: Vim-style Connect Mode (PASSING)
- Implemented full Vim-style edge creation workflow:
  1. Press C with node selected → enters Connect mode, source = selected node
  2. Press C without selection → enters Connect mode, must pick source first
  3. Arrow keys in Connect mode → spatial navigation to pick target node
  4. Enter → confirms target → shows type picker
  5. 1/2/3 keys → picks edge type (1=Sync, 2=Async, 3=Data Flow)
  6. Edge created, undo snapshot taken, returns to Normal mode, new edge selected
  7. Escape at any step → cancels, clears state, returns to Normal

- Added to uiStore:
  - connectSource, connectTarget, connectStep state
  - startConnect(), setConnectTarget(), setConnectStep(), clearConnectState() actions
  - exitToNormal() now also clears connect state

- Modified Canvas.tsx:
  - Connect mode keyboard handler (arrow keys, Enter, 1/2/3) in capture phase
  - Normal arrow handler skips when in Connect mode
  - Preview dashed edge (animated, blue, strokeDasharray) from source to target
  - Source node green glow CSS class (connect-source-glow)

SESSION: 2026-03-04 - Feature #267
==================================================

## What was accomplished:

### Feature #267: Idempotent dev server launcher script (PASSING)

Created scripts/ensure-dev-server.sh - an idempotent launcher that ensures exactly
one Vite dev server is running on port 5173:

**Script features:**
- Health check: curl to localhost:5173, exits 0 immediately if server already running
- Atomic lock: mkdir-based lock prevents concurrent launches (race-condition safe)
- Double-check after lock: re-checks port after acquiring lock
- Background startup: nohup npm run dev, polls until ready (max 30s, 0.5s intervals)
- Process monitoring: detects if server process dies during startup
- PID file tracking: stores PID for reliable stop
- --stop flag: kills running server via PID file or lsof fallback
- Cleanup: lock auto-removed via trap EXIT

**Configuration changes:**
1. vite.config.ts: Added `strictPort: true` - Vite now errors if port 5173 is taken
   instead of silently using 5174+
2. package.json: Added `dev:ensure` and `dev:stop` npm scripts
3. playwright.config.ts: webServer.command changed from `npm run dev` to `npm run dev:ensure`

**Testing completed:**
- First run: starts server successfully (exit 0)
- Idempotency: 5 sequential runs all exit 0 without spawning new processes
- Stop/restart: `dev:stop` kills server, `dev:ensure` restarts it
- strictPort: Second Vite on port 5173 fails with "Port 5173 is already in use"
- Lock bypass: Script detects running server before checking lock (fast path)
- Browser verification: App loads correctly at localhost:5173
- Console: 0 errors, 0 warnings
- All 3242 existing tests pass (155 test files)
- No mock data patterns in production code

### Feature #299: Node.js File System Adapter (PASSING)
- Created src/core/platform/nodeFileSystemAdapter.ts:
  - NodeFileSystemAdapter implements FileSystemAdapter interface
  - Uses Node.js `fs` module for read/write operations (dynamic imports)
  - pickFile(): reads from constructor path, returns PickFileResult
  - readFile(path): reads from any path with error handling
  - saveFile(data, handle?): writes to handle path or constructor path, creates parent dirs
  - saveFileAs(data, suggestedName): writes to new path, creates parent dirs
  - shareFile(data, filename): writes file to disk (no share sheet in CLI)
  - fileExists(path): convenience method for checking file existence
  - NodeFileSystemError class with code (ENOENT/EACCES/EISDIR/ENOSPC) and filePath
  - Graceful error wrapping for all filesystem errors
  - All paths resolved to absolute via path.resolve()
- 42 unit tests covering:
  - Constructor, pickFile, readFile, saveFile, saveFileAs, shareFile

## Session: Feature #304 - CLI Query Commands
Date: 2026-03-04

### Feature #304: CLI Query Commands (describe, list-nodes, get-node, search, list-nodedefs) - PASSING

#### What was already implemented:
- src/cli/commands/query.ts: All 5 query commands with registerQueryCommands()
- src/cli/index.ts: Same 5 commands inline (duplicate)
- test/unit/cli/queryCommands.test.ts: 37 tests

#### Issues found and fixed:
1. **Diagnostic log pollution**: console.log from [TextApi], [RegistryManager], [ExportApi]
   constructors was going to stdout, breaking JSON pipe output.
   - Added suppressDiagnosticLogs() in src/cli/index.ts that redirects [bracketed] logs to stderr
   - Applied in loadContext() and list-nodedefs command
   - Applied same fix in src/cli/commands/query.ts

2. **Protobuf ESM import**: src/proto/archcanvas.pb.js used `import * as $protobuf from "protobufjs/minimal"`
   which doesn't work in Node.js ESM (tsx). Changed to `import $protobufDefault from "protobufjs/minimal"`
   with CJS→ESM normalization.

3. **Test fixture bug**: queryCommands.test.ts used `targetNodeId` instead of `nodeId` in addNote params.

#### Verification:
- All 37 query command tests passing
- All 148 CLI tests passing (57 entry point + 37 query + 54 context)

  - `archcanvas describe --file f.archc --format json` ✓

## Session: Feature #340 - Filesystem Scanner with Gitignore Support
Date: 2026-03-04

### Feature #340: Filesystem Scanner with Gitignore Support - PASSING

#### Implementation:
Created src/analyze/scanner.ts with a complete filesystem scanning module:

- **parseGitignore(content)**: Parses .gitignore file content into structured rules
  - Handles comments, empty lines, negation (!), directory-only patterns (trailing /)
  - Converts gitignore glob patterns to RegExp (supports *, **, ?, [])
  - Handles escaped characters and path-relative vs basename matching

- **isIgnored(relativePath, isDirectory, rules)**: Tests if a path matches ignore rules
  - Processes rules in order, last match wins (supports negation override)
  - Respects directory-only patterns

- **scanDirectory(rootPath, options)**: Main entry point
  - Recursive directory walking using Node.js fs APIs
  - Merges .gitignore rules at each directory level
  - Built-in ignores: node_modules, .git, dist, build, __pycache__, target, vendor, etc.
  - Configurable: maxDepth (default 10), maxFiles (default 10000), additionalIgnore patterns
  - Returns ScanResult: { fileTree, totalFiles, totalDirs, languageBreakdown }
  - FileTree has nested DirectoryEntry/FileEntry structure
  - Each FileEntry has: name, relativePath, size, extension, lastModified
  - Sorted entries for deterministic output

#### Tests (test/unit/analyze/scanner.test.ts):
- 26 tests all passing
- parseGitignore: simple patterns, comments, negation, escaped chars
- isIgnored: filenames, directory-only, negation, path separators, **, ?
- scanDirectory: simple files, nested dirs, metadata, built-in ignores, .gitignore respect,
  nested .gitignore, maxDepth, maxFiles, additionalIgnore, language breakdown,
  relative paths, empty dirs, sorting, defaults, non-existent dir

#### Committed: 9275b77
#### Features passing: 332+ of 340+

## Session: Feature #341 - Project Type and Framework Detector
Date: 2026-03-04

### Feature #341: Project Type and Framework Detector - PASSING

#### Implementation:
Created src/analyze/detector.ts with comprehensive project analysis capabilities:

- **detectLanguages(scanResult)**: Detects languages from file extension distribution and config files (package.json→JS/TS, go.mod→Go, Cargo.toml→Rust, requirements.txt→Python, pom.xml→Java, etc.)
- **detectFrameworks(scanResult)**: Detects frameworks from config files (Next.js, Vite, Angular, Django, Spring Boot, etc.) and file extensions (.tsx→React, .vue→Vue, .svelte→Svelte)
- **detectProjectType(scanResult)**: Classifies as monorepo (lerna/turbo/nx/workspaces), microservices (multiple Dockerfiles), library, or single-app
- **detectBuildSystems(scanResult)**: Identifies npm, yarn, pnpm, cargo, go modules, maven, gradle, make, etc.
- **detectInfraSignals(scanResult)**: Detects Docker, Kubernetes, Terraform, CI/CD (GitHub Actions, GitLab, Jenkins, CircleCI, Travis), cloud platforms
- **detectDataStores(scanResult)**: Finds Prisma, Drizzle, SQLite, TypeORM, Knex, Firebase, Protocol Buffers
- **detectEntryPoints(scanResult)**: Identifies common entry points (src/index.ts, main.go, manage.py, etc.)
- **detectProject(scanResult)**: Main API returning complete ProjectProfile

#### Types exported:
- ProjectProfile, DetectedLanguage, DetectedFramework, ProjectType, InfraSignal, DetectedDataStore

#### Tests:
- test/unit/analyze/detector.test.ts: 72 tests covering all detection functions
- All 98 analyze tests passing (72 detector + 26 scanner)
- Committed: d105b08

#### Current completion status:
- Feature #341 marked passing

## Session: Feature #342 - Key File Selector and Content Extractor
Date: 2026-03-04

### Feature #342: Key File Selector and Content Extractor - PASSING

#### Implementation:
Created src/analyze/fileSelector.ts with intelligent file selection and content extraction:

- **selectKeyFiles(scanResult, projectProfile, options)**: Main API function
  - 4-tier priority system for file selection:
    - Tier 1 (always include): package.json, go.mod, Cargo.toml, Dockerfile, docker-compose.yml, README.md, tsconfig.json, etc.
    - Tier 2 (high value): entry points (src/index.ts, main.go, etc.), route definitions (routes.ts, urls.py), schema files (.proto, .graphql, openapi.yaml, schema.prisma)
    - Tier 3 (structural): module index files (index.ts, __init__.py, mod.rs)
    - Tier 4 (representative): 1-2 sample source files per major directory
  - Smart content truncation: reads up to maxLinesPerFile (default 500), adds truncation notice
  - Token budget: caps total extracted content at totalTokenBudget (default 100K tokens)
  - Deduplication: files classified in multiple tiers are only included once at highest priority
  - Configurable via FileSelectionOptions: maxLinesPerFile, totalTokenBudget, rootDir, skipContentRead

- **Types exported**: FileTier, SelectedFile, KeyFileSet, FileSelectionOptions

#### Tests (test/unit/analyze/fileSelector.test.ts):
- 44 tests all passing
- Tier 1: package.json, go.mod, Cargo.toml, Dockerfile, docker-compose.yml, README.md, tsconfig.json, multiple Tier 1 files
- Tier 2: entry points (src/index.ts, main.go, main.py), detected entry points from profile, route definitions (routes.ts, router.js, urls.py), schema files (.proto, .graphql, openapi.yaml, schema.prisma)
- Tier 3: index.ts barrels, __init__.py, mod.rs, index.js
- Tier 4: representative files, 2-per-dir limit, no duplication with higher tiers, source-only filtering
- Token budget: respects limit, default 100K, provides totalTokenEstimate
- Tier ordering: 1 before 2, 2 before 3, priority on tight budget
- Return format: KeyFileSet structure, empty scan handling
- Multi-project types: Node.js/TS, Go, Python, Rust
- Deduplication and options tests

#### Verification:
- 142 total analyze tests passing (44 new + 72 detector + 26 scanner)
- Build succeeds cleanly
- No mock data patterns in production code
- Committed: d8780e8

#### Current completion status:
- Feature #342 marked passing
- Features passing: 342 of 349 (98.0%)

## Session: Feature #343 - AI Architecture Inference Engine
Date: 2026-03-04

### Feature #343: AI Architecture Inference Engine - PASSING

#### Implementation:
Created src/analyze/inferEngine.ts with comprehensive AI-powered architecture inference:

- **inferArchitecture(sender, projectProfile, keyFiles, options)**: Main API function
  - Takes an AIMessageSender (dependency injection for testability)
  - Takes ProjectProfile from detector.ts and KeyFileSet from fileSelector.ts
  - Returns InferenceResult with nodes, edges, architecture name/description

- **Analysis Depth Modes**:
  - 'quick': Single prompt, structure-only analysis (1 AI call)
  - 'standard': Multi-step analysis (3 AI calls): identify components → relationships → map to types
  - 'deep': Standard + refinement step (4 AI calls): adds detailed notes and suggestions

- **Zod Validation**: inferenceResultSchema validates AI responses with recursive node schema
  - InferredNode: id, type, displayName, description, codeRefs[], children[] (recursive)
  - InferredEdge: from, to, type (SYNC/ASYNC/DATA_FLOW), label
  - InferredCodeRef: path, role (SOURCE/API_SPEC/SCHEMA/DEPLOYMENT/CONFIG/TEST)
  - Step-specific schemas for intermediate validation

- **extractJson()**: Robust JSON extraction from AI text (handles markdown fences, surrounding text)
- **batchFiles()**: Splits files into batches that fit within token limits
- **mergeResults()**: Deduplicates and merges results from multiple inference batches
- **sendWithRetry()**: Exponential backoff retry logic (configurable maxRetries, 30s max delay)
- **Streaming**: onProgress callback for step-by-step progress, onChunk for text streaming
- **Abort support**: AbortSignal propagation through all async operations

- **AIMessageSender interface**: Dependency injection for the AI client
  - Allows testing without real API calls
  - Compatible with existing src/ai/client.ts sendMessage function

- **Built-in Node Types**: All 15 node types included in prompts:
  - Compute: service, function, worker, api-gateway
  - Data: database, cache, object-storage, repository
  - Messaging: message-queue, event-bus, stream-processor
  - Network: load-balancer, cdn
  - Observability: logging, monitoring

#### Tests (test/unit/analyze/inferEngine.test.ts): 49 tests
- extractJson: plain text, markdown fences, nested objects, surrounding text
- batchFiles: single batch, multi-batch, oversized files, empty input
- mergeResults: single result, dedup nodes/edges, architecture name from first
- inferenceResultSchema: valid data, missing fields, empty nodes, invalid edge types, recursive children, code ref roles
- inferArchitecture quick: valid result, single call, project profile in prompt, node types in prompt, file contents, markdown fences, progress events, streaming
- inferArchitecture standard: 3 AI calls, progress events per step, partial results
- inferArchitecture deep: 4 AI calls, step 4 refinement event
- Error handling: invalid JSON, schema validation, raw response in errors, retry logic, max retries exceeded, abort signal
- Token batching: multi-batch merge in quick mode
- Profile formatting: infra signals, data stores, empty profile

#### Verification:
- 191 total analyze tests passing (49 new + 142 existing)
- TypeScript compiles with no errors (tsc --noEmit)
- No mock data patterns in production code
- Committed: c2a6bdc

#### Current completion status:
- Feature #343 marked passing
- Features passing: 343 of 349 (98.3%)

## Session: Feature #366 - Node text remains readable across all color tints and themes
Date: 2026-03-05

### Feature #366: Node text readable across all color tints and themes - PASSING

#### Analysis:
Performed comprehensive text contrast analysis across all 12 accent colors (Blue, Green, Orange, Purple, Cyan, Red, Pink, Indigo, Teal, Amber, Lime, Rose) in both dark and light modes.

Key findings:
1. All icon badge contrast ratios >= 3.0:1 (WCAG AA for large text) via getContrastColor()
2. All header wash text contrast ratios >= 12:1 (excellent) because tint opacity is only 18% max
3. All text tokens (text-text, text-muted-foreground, text-subtle) are theme-aware and switch properly
4. NodeBadges uses dark: Tailwind variants which needed proper wiring to the .dark class

#### Bug found and resolved:
Tailwind CSS 4 dark mode variant not wired to .dark class.
NodeBadges.tsx uses dark:text-blue-400, dark:text-amber-400, dark:text-emerald-400.
Tailwind CSS 4 defaults dark: to @media (prefers-color-scheme: dark), not class-based.
The app uses .dark class on html (set by ThemeProvider).
Without @custom-variant dark, badge text colors would follow system preference instead of app theme.
Resolution: Added @custom-variant dark to src/index.css

#### Visual Verification (5 themes tested):
1. Dark theme: Service (blue), Object Storage (lime), Message Queue (orange) - all text readable
2. Light theme: All 7 node types (blue, green, purple, orange, purple/cloud, lime, cyan) - all readable
3. Rose Pine Dawn (light): 3 nodes tested - all text readable
4. Nord (dark): 3 nodes tested - all text readable
5. Catppuccin Mocha (dark): 3 nodes tested - all text readable

#### Text elements verified:
- Display names (text-text)
- Type labels (text-muted-foreground on bg-highlight-med)
- Argument keys (text-muted-foreground)
- Argument values (text-subtle)
- Icon badges (getContrastColor auto-contrast)
- Badge colors (dark: variant now correctly wired)

#### Build: Clean (no CSS or new TypeScript errors)
#### Commit: 8ede9ee
#### Feature #366 marked passing

- Press any other key while Cmd held → overlay dismissed, timer cancelled
